Auras can also be diagnosed with the help of quartz pendulums or with\nsensitized hands. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The first aura layer extends\ntwo inches outside the body. </span><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;</span><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">It deals\nwith </span><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;</span><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">sensations as pain, heat and cold.\nThe colour of the aura on this level ranges from fine, thin light aqua blue for\nquiet and sensitive people to coarse, deep bluish-gray for strong people. The\nhealth of the first layer determines our potential for enjoying physical life.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The second aura layer\nrepresents your self esteem. Images for this layer range from brightly coloured\nclouds (positive feelings) to dark shades (negative feelings). These clouds of\nenergy flow along the energy lines of the first layer. If you stop the flow of\nthese feelings, you stop the flow of the clouds, and they become dark and\nsluggish. A stagnant second layer can impede the flow of the first and third\nlayers.&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The third layer\nrepresents logic and clarity, with which we think and desire to learn new\nthings. The energy lines here are fine and thin, lemon yellow in colour and\npulsate at a very high rate. A dull layer shows dullness of mind and\ndisinclination to think. Negative thoughts correlate with slower pulsations of\nthe field in this region and dark, distorted energy lines. </span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The fourth layer\nrepresents our feelings for the people we relate to. This level is the bridge\nbetween our physical world (experienced through our first three layers) and the\nspiritual world (experienced through the next three). The energy here is thick\nand fluid, and it vibrates faster than the second layer. An unhealthy fourth\nlayer is dark and heavy, with the consistency of mucus. The energy of the\nfourth layer flows between people as they interact; streams of </span><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;</span><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">bioplasmic energy move out from your layer\ntowards the other person\u2019s field.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">These streams can be soft and rosy between\nlovers; dark, sticky and gray-green when one is jealous; high-peaked orange-red\nfor one burning with passion; or dark-red and pointed when one is angry. We are\nborn with cords connecting us with our parents, representing our relationships\nwith our parents and determining the kinds of relationships we form with the\nmen and women in our lives. Each new relationship develops more cords.</span><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The fifth layer two\nfeet away from the body represents the divine will, and is associated with the\npower of words in the creative process. It is by accessing this layer that what\nwe wish or say to ourselves comes true in the physical world. Those with an\nunderdeveloped fifth layer have trouble keeping their lives in order; they\ncannot figure out their purpose in life. Those with a developed fifth layer are\npunctual, good planners and good executors of their plans. They have a sense of\npurpose in their lives. The fifth level has grooves or slots for the bluish\nenergy lines of the first layer.</span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The sixth layer\nrepresents divine love and ecstasy. Here are the feelings we experience when we\nfall in love with someone, get lost in the beauty of a landscape and so forth.\nExtending two to two-and-three-quarters feet from the body, the sixth kosha is\na gold-silver halo of light.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Our need at this level is for spiritual\nnourishment through experiences that make us feel lost in something -- we might\nfeel connected to the stars, the trees, the ocean or everything out there in\nthe universe -- thus giving us the experience of oneness. This is the level we\nexperience in deep meditation. This level comprises streams of light of various\ncolours, radiating in all directions at a high frequency. The beams may be\nstraight or sagging, depending upon the health of this level.&nbsp;</span><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The seventh layer\nrepresents the divine mind, and is made up of&nbsp; high-frequency, bright\ngolden energy lines. Repetition of the bija manta LANG deepens\nconcentration, giving awareness and inner strength. Its vibrations create a\npassage inside the Brahma Nadi. Brahma Nadi, is the subtle channel through\nwhich the Kundalini, when awakened moves from Muladhara to Sahasrara Chakra.\nThe element associated with the Muladhara Chakra is Earth. The square is the\nsymbol for Earth. When the bija mantra VANG is repeated it enhances the production and\ncirculation of fluids in the body. The shape associated with this element is\nthe circle, which represents the element water. Water droplets are spherical.\nWater is the essence of life. Sounding the bija mantra YANG gives one control\nover air, prana and the breath. The bija mantra YANG is the sound form of the\ndeity Vayu, the lord of the air/wind. The Anahata Chakra is associated with the\nsix-pointed star which is made up of two triangles. The one pointing upwards\nsymbolises Shiva, the male principal. The other triangle points downward symbolising\nShakti, the female principal--stolen by the Jews.&nbsp; The six-pointed star also symbolises the\nbalancing of energy in the Heart chakra, which lies between the three chakras\nabove it and the three chakras below it. The Anahata Chakra is associated with\nlove and the desire for sharing and sympathy. Here energy can move upward or\ndownward. The element associated with the Anahata Chakra is vayu (air or wind).\nVayu is thevital life-giving force (prana). It aids the functions of the lungs\nand heart, circulating fresh oxygen and vital energy.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 18.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><b>\u201cHAM\u201d- Vishudha chakra\n5 (throat)</b><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">The bija mantra for\nthis chakra is HAM sounded as HANG. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "14", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/7450636914407978405/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "5581019134560482517", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2011-02-05T09:34:00+05:30", "updated": "2011-09-25T15:24:08+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxMzE2OTQ0NDQ4OTc3Cm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2011/02/naive-sailor-winch-brake-rendering-capt.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/5581019134560482517", "title": "THE NAIVE SAILOR , WINCH BRAKE RENDERING--  CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUzLWufjuAI/AAAAAAAADSE/0ef8vXN2rfY/s1600/images+%25281%2529+%25281%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUzLWufjuAI/AAAAAAAADSE/0ef8vXN2rfY/s1600/images+%25281%2529+%25281%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\nOn one of my ships, i received a general circular from the company , that the bow stopper must NOT be put after anchoring, and that ship should put a red flag on the gypsy--so that -- hold your breath-- the wheelhouse OOW can come to know when the windlass brake renders ( SIC!!). <br />\n<br />\nThey went on and on in about 18 pages to warn us that if we don't do that, the anchor chain will snap!. And they made a nice video to back their claim. The stupid video had more video graphic content that seamanship content, and it would WOW a retarded 8 year old. &nbsp;&nbsp;It was amusing to see the anchor cable moving like an anaconda, disregarding the damping effects of seawater and force of gravity.<br />\n<br />\nI wasted no time in being most sarcastic , ( you should never be civil to fools who put sailors lives in danger even if he is related to the almighty queen ) and telling them that the red flag was first introduced to the blue high seas in 1992 by the Russian bunker river operating &nbsp;barge pretenders who came out to sea with forged certificates.<br />\n<br />\nI declared categorically that i would NOT follow this bullshit (with a capital B ) circular, nor will anybody at sea--and that all the ship staff is already sniggering over this fantastic circular, written by the stupid DPA.<br />\n<br />\nI myself have done thousands of anchorings over 28 years in command with, &nbsp;100% success rate , on different types of ships , in different locations, in different weather conditions--unlike pilots who are one trick ponies.<br />\n<br />\nRendering can be tolerated for static braking like the mooring hawser winches--but NEVER EVER for a dynamic high speed gypsy like the anchor windlass.<br />\n<br />\nImagine a ULCC being held by the windlass brake!<br />\n<br />\n-- what is the principle of the windlass? -- FRICTION right?. You plan to hold a loaded ULCC in an anchorage with swell , with the ship yawing wildly, using friction? <br />\n<br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">The bow stopper must always be put. First ensure there is NO half twist between the gypsy and the stopper, as is usual.</span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUzLkdKRHQI/AAAAAAAADSI/wc2a-RHB5CE/s1600/download.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUzLkdKRHQI/AAAAAAAADSI/wc2a-RHB5CE/s1600/download.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\nThis rendering thing is the biggest bullshit going on at sea.<br />\n<br />\nOn bulk carriers with crane and grabs , which tend to get buried under cargo slides, we test the cranes to proof load . On old ships the brake lining surface and the abutting surface crevice is flushed with carbon remover to get rid of the slippery heat generated graphite layer. Then we tone up the relief valve before the class surveyor comes. The tank is filled with sea water to the required weight . After lifting the proof weight the runner joystick has to be suddenly put to neutral and the crane hook must not creep downwards due to gravity --the automatic brake must grip. &nbsp;After the test is over we usually tone down the relief valve to the safe working load again. So if the grab gets buried due to a landslide , the relief valve will lift.<br />\n<br />\nRendering of mooring winches can be done easily ( for the first layer ) with automatic brakes. On manual brakes the torque meter is used on the handle. <span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">All this is OK for a split drum which affords only one single layer.</span><br />\n<br />\nBut what about a usual mooring winch drum, where a hawser of 220 metres is wound . It will have minimum 8 layers. When you send the first line ashore or cast off the last line, it will usually be a spring, with 30 metres out on the jetty bollard and the remaining 190 metres in 7 layers on the reel.<br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">Where is the intelligence is doing a brake rendering test on the first layer, for manual brakes once in a year? How relevant is the rendering set point after 365 days?. </span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-j_cJF9ppim4/Tn76L-WqdqI/AAAAAAAAGhg/gDcoxPP5DnY/s1600/ndw.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-j_cJF9ppim4/Tn76L-WqdqI/AAAAAAAAGhg/gDcoxPP5DnY/s1600/ndw.gif\" /></a></div><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">It requires a real IDIOT to think, that the brake lining thickness will not reduce, due to wear. Will the the friction coefficient between the metal abutting surface and the brake lining be the same in dry and wet weather?</span><br />\n<br />\n(These are the same pathetic jokers who wanted NIL vaccum with 100% recirc, or NIL fresh air intake, &nbsp;for accomodation AC at oil terminals, with the toilet and galley exhaust fans running merrily.)<br />\n<br />\nThe forward brake abutting bands on the rotating gypsy is the most under maintained area on the ship. This area can never be painted. On better ships this brake abutting area has a stainless steel veneer. If any salt water ( electrolyte ) enters this crevice it forms a galvanic cell between the brass countersunk bolt heads of the brake lining and the steel gypsy. This galvanically weakens the steel.<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"> The surface may look pristine , but it is molecularly weakened.</span> If you chip with a sharp hammer, chunks will break off, like a clay pot. Rendering brings out iron powder .<br />\n<br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">If the brake renders heat is produced. The heat produces slippery graphite , and it continues slipping.</span><br />\n<br />\nAnd nowadays on almost all old ships we find different grades of rope being sent on board --all having the same material on the certificate. But the breaking load will be different. And 60% of this value is what the brake is rendering set point.<br />\n<br />\nOk you have 4 ropes on the winch reel and the remaining 3 are on the mooring bitt, as a figure of eight . How are we gonna render these ropes on the bitt?. <span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">So you give step motherly treatment to 40% ropes--where is the intelligence?</span><br />\n<br />\nThe modern light hawsers do NOT have a friction coefficient ( like the old polypropylene hawsers ) and they slip with a jerk, despite taking two round turns on each bitt and then putting a figure of eight and then again taking full rounds. When hawsers slip with a jerk, they always break. Very rarely can a constant pull break ropes. Anchor chains also break easily when it jerks.<br />\n<br />\nEver noticed how three tiny Yokohama fenders protect the ship side hulls of two loaded supertankers alongside each other . It is because there is NO sharp bang or surge or jerk or hammer. Remove these fenders and the steel hulls will crumple like paper.<br />\n<br />\nI have taken several deliveries, where the Yard does the first rendering tests. You should see the sheepish look on the face of the man in charge. He knows he has to pull the wool over his own eyes as well as others. Well the ship need this certificate-- without this we will be detained by any inspector.<br />\n<br />\nAfter you tighten the windlass brake band after anchoring , check how many spare threads are available on the brake handle .<br />\n<br />\nThe brass countersunk bolt heads must never come in contact with the gypsy steel. Metal to metal has less friction. And even if it makes contact the brass bolt head will wear off--while a steel bolt can cause havoc. There can be no steel to steel friction , and the steel bolt head will groove the galvanically weakened gypsy abutting surface.<br />\n<br />\nWe all play along , and tell the naked emperor--such nice clothes you wear, mE lord!. Nobody has the will to call the bluff. &nbsp;We deserve to be ruled by fools ashore.<br />\n<br />\nThis is why millions our rat guards fell off for the past 300 years and millions will fall off for the next 300 years.<br />\n<br />\nThis is why we use the loud hailer cone on the bridge is applied on the mouth for shouting stupid orders. It is actually meant for putting it on your ear and finding out to min 5 deg accuracy, the direction of the foghorn you hear at sea on the bridge wings. In Titanic if the stupid British officers had applied the load hailer to their ears , to find the direction of &nbsp;lifejacket whistles , instead of their big mouths shouting \" Any body there ?\" they could have saved more passengers from the freezing water.<br />\n<br />\nAdvise: &nbsp;If you have drums with 8 layers of hawser turns, it is better to make sure you last lines to cast off forward and aft is a rope from the mooring bitts ( especially if the current and the wind can put the ship in trouble ). They never get stuck.<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUzIG9n3N3I/AAAAAAAADSA/vFLbAllgmJc/s1600/aji.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUzIG9n3N3I/AAAAAAAADSA/vFLbAllgmJc/s1600/aji.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\nCAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL<br />\n..<br />\n<br />\n<br />\n<br />\n</div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "8", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/5581019134560482517/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "986396662734298330", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2011-02-05T00:33:00+05:30", "updated": "2017-07-04T09:49:11+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxNDk5MTQxOTUxMTYzCm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2011/02/naive-sailor-gps-capt-ajit-vadakayil.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/986396662734298330", "title": "THE NAIVE SAILOR, GPS -- CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUxFzPN5C_I/AAAAAAAADR4/46Z4gNgaOd4/s1600/images+%25281%2529+%25281%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUxFzPN5C_I/AAAAAAAADR4/46Z4gNgaOd4/s1600/images+%25281%2529+%25281%2529.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\nWhen i first commanded a ship 28 years ago, my ship did NOT have a Satellite Navigator. We took celestial sights with sextant.<br />\n<br />\nSo i wrote to the Chairman of the company ( a political post ), telling him to stop all these bullshit seminars for saving fuel.<br />\n<br />\nI made it clear that the shortest distance between 2 points on a globe , is a Great circle or a rhumb line.<br />\n<br />\nHe replied to my letter and said , he will ensure all ships will soon have a Satellite Navigator.<br />\n<br />\nSo my next ship had a American NCS dinosaur Satellite navigator which gave only about 16 positions a day at the equator, and maybe 50 positions a day in very high latitudes. The accuracy was poor.<br />\n<br />\nI got a GPS on my ship only as late as 1990. &nbsp;So as soon as it was fitted i gave orders to start a new style GPS log. It contained the following columns.<br />\n<br />\nDate/ time in SMT and GPS UTC ( recordings at every 30 minutes max interval )<br />\nLat/ Long<br />\nGPS speed<br />\nGPS course made good<br />\nPropeller speed<br />\nGyro course steered<br />\nWGS84 correction applied Yes/ No<br />\nRemarks/ Sign<br />\n<br />\nEven in 2010 i had the same format GPS log.<br />\n<br />\nAll vetting inspectors , PSC , Shore powers consider it a crime if the OOW trusts the GPS. They say-don't trust the dang thing.<br />\n<br />\nCapt Vadakayil says-<br />\n<span style=\"font-size: large;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><br /></b></span>\n<span style=\"font-size: large;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\">&nbsp;<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">\"<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: xx-small;\"> YOU CAN TRUST YOUR GPS , PROVIDED YOUR COMPARE :--</span></span></b></span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: large;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><br />\n</b></span></span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: large;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\">THE GPS COURSE WITH GYRO COURSE -- CORRECTED FOR ERROR&nbsp;</b></span></span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: large;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><br /></b></span></span>\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: large;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\">THE GPS SPEED WITH PROPELLER SPEED -- ALLOWED FOR WEATHER</b></span></span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: large;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><br /></b></span></span>\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: large;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\">AND WGS 84 CORRECTION.</b></span></span><br />\n<br />\nIf the GPS gives wrong positions , the comparison will be haywire-- absolutely. GPS pings the ship every few seconds, if the speed and course don't change this means your antenna has fallen off. So many ships have run aground because they were on the DR mode as GPS did NOT give any inputs.<br />\n<br />\nThere are 31 active GPS satellites plus 2 spare ones at a height of 19300 kms. You just need 4 for a trilaterated fix. They make 2 circles of the earth every day.<br />\n<br />\nOn two ships , on the very first day I found a difference of 5 degrees between the GPS course and Gyro course at sea , with smooth weather, prompting me to take an amplitude of the sun. And then i get a gyro error of 5 degrees --this means all and sundry were deliberately giving bull in the gyro error log.<br />\n<br />\nOn both these ships ( both had finished 2 years of sea voyages since delivery ) i got the master gyro foundation bolts loosened at the next port and turned it using a shore bearing, and re tightened it. For calling a Gyro technician would be of no use.<br />\n<br />\nPeople say GPS will stop working during sun flares, Well since i got my first GPS , it has NOT let me down except twice at Sicily ( gun runners jamming using Soviet jammers) during the Serb war.<br />\n<br />\nAnd then once i joined a fast container ship capable of doing 26 knots. The Japanese Engineering owners superintendents were very nasty and arrogant men , who used to treat the previous Chief Engineers, Masters and Tech Managers Tech Engr&nbsp;Suptds in a shabby manner. It had a racist tinge.<br />\n<br />\n&nbsp;I saw lengthy correspondence when i went to the company HO for pre-joining briefing. Even the MD asked me to take care not to overload the engines and get the squeamish Japs upset. And then they went around explaining a stupid Jap load envelop main engine power diagram.<br />\n<br />\nSoon enough i get a stinker after one noon message from the Jap owners ( their name sounds like what you wear on your feet ), accusing me of overloading their precious engine.<br />\n<br />\nI gave them such a severe bollocking by email-- that they let us alone after that, for ever.<br />\n<br />\nNo more taking out frustrations on ship, by these split personalities. ( ever seen a Jap blue movie?--it is all the same!-- it is NOT about making love, it is about torturing the poor girl and making her cry and whimper ).<br />\n<span style=\"background-color: white; font-size: large;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"background-color: white; font-size: large;\">I wasted no time in telling them that their load diagram and power calculations has NIL intelligence.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"background-color: white; font-size: large;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"background-color: white; font-size: large;\">&nbsp;I said , that i use my GPS to find out the engine load <b><span style=\"color: red;\">every second</span></b>--NOT every 24 hours at noon .</span><br />\n<br />\nThe GPS immediately tells you &nbsp;the engine load, even if your propeller gets caught in a fishing nets or if a large helm is given at 26 knots. My standing orders on bridge contained the sentence \" If the difference between GPS speed and Propeller speed exceeds by so many percent, i must be informed\".<br />\n<br />\nAt anchor put the GPS and the radar into plotter mode, and the pattern tells you the way the ship behaves ,and also how the anchor is holding. You can zoom in to few metres . So next time when the stupid pilot wants the GPS speed while approaching berth, on a turning ship, caution him it is the speed of the GPS whip antenna over the ground--NOT the ship as a whole.<br />\n<br />\nThe GPS and the radar must always be used in a man overboard situation , by pressing the MOB button and then going on plotter mode.<br />\n<br />\nI bought my own Magellan portable GPS from a US naval store at Honolulu, in 1984. Nowadays i don't carry &nbsp;my GPS on board as we have several GPS sets hooked on to almost every GMDSS set.<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUxG-n70U8I/AAAAAAAADR8/id2YQCByA_g/s1600/images+%252811%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUxG-n70U8I/AAAAAAAADR8/id2YQCByA_g/s1600/images+%252811%2529.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\nIndia will put her own 7 GPS satellites ( IRNSS ) &nbsp;by 2016, making her the 4th country in the world to have it.<br />\n<br />\n<br />\nDigression: Only ignorant engineers calculate ME power from Turbocharger parameters. The best way is to use the fuel rack method.<br />\n<br />\nEXAMPLE:<br />\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nFormula for engine output: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />\n<br />\nLe&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nHua&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;= Lower calorific value of fuel oil in the ship (kJ/kg or kcal/kg)<o:p></o:p></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nHu&nbsp;&nbsp; This as as stupid as writing volumes about fishing boats in the ship's wake.<br />\n<br />\nAt sea on the bridge we care only about fishing boats ahead of ship. We like to be PRO-ACTIVE and deal with <span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">hazards</span> which have NOT yet happened. We like to talk about coming shadows.<br />\n<br />\nBut the jokers ashore don't want this on SMS reporting records, for if the shadow indeed does its evil deed, they stand to lose their honourable chairs.<br />\n<br />\nThey will even give you fancy ROOT CAUSE analysis tools, where as soon as the blame comes on the sailor's incompetence or negligence , it stops . And then the poor sailor is victimised.<br />\n<br />\nSo why did the third mate have a collision?<br />\n<br />\nThe root cause arrives by the RCA software says he slept on the bridge , which is a crime, and the third mate did NOT follow watch keeping company orders as per the manual.<br />\n<br />\nYou sailors must take this further.<br />\n<br />\n<i>Here is a true case , of an European Third mate, who sailed with me.</i><br />\n<i><br />\n</i><br />\n<i>Why did the third mate fall asleep?---He could NOT sleep in his rest hours.</i><br />\n<i><br />\n</i><br />\n<i>Why could he not sleep?-- Because he was very worried</i><br />\n<i><br />\n</i><br />\n<i>Why was he worried ?-- Because his best friend told him that his wife was seen in a pick up bar.</i><br />\n<i><br />\n</i><br />\n<i>Why was his wife --? --because her husband has NOT send his salary allotment for past 3 months.</i><br />\n<i><br />\n</i><br />\n<i>Why did the allotment --- ? --because the company did not remit the allotment.</i><br />\n<i><br />\n</i><br />\n<i>Why did the company---? --because the owners did not send the funds despite 10 reminders.</i><br />\n<i><br />\n</i><br />\n<i>SO THE <span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">ROOT CAUSE</span> IS -- THE RICH OWNERS DID NOT SEND FUNDS.</i><br />\n<br />\nThese are the same rich owners who try to skim 10 Dollars off you. You take a flight, the airhostess will wait on you. After the plane lands, she heads off to a swank 5 star hotel and you go to a cheap sleazy motel.<br />\n<br />\nThe shore powers would like to give you a safety belt to be tied around your waist. As soon as you fall off from a height you will break your spine --100%. &nbsp;Who cares? <br />\n<br />\nIt is upon the sailor to demand for a safety harness which supports you at the crotch, so that you don't break your spine. Be aware. You owe it to yourself.<br />\n<br />\nA lot of boiler explosions and Generator trips at sea go unreported. The company does NOT want this on the records. You try to put a SMS report about a AE trip while picking up pilot , and immediately you will get victimised.<br />\n<br />\nConrods of AE have been busting for a hundred years-- who cares?<br />\n<br />\nHas anybody found the root cause for prevention? LSGO OF LOW FLASH POINT/ LOW VISC / <br />\nHIGH CETANE WITH LOW CALORIFIC VALUE &nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n---</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br />\n</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nCONSIDER TIMING OF 4 STROKE ON FCOL AS A 3D ANIMATION <br />\nIN YOUR MANN&nbsp;MANDIR :</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: x-small;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nSTROKE 1 downwards INTAKE &nbsp;:--</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nFUEL is injected a &nbsp;7.5 deg before TDC and and <br />\ncontinues to maybe 40 deg&nbsp; after TDC-- depending on <br />\nignition lag. ( very little for a low flash&nbsp; point automative <br />\nfuel clandestinely palmed off to ship as marine diesel&nbsp;fuel )</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nFRESH AIR &nbsp;is taken in from turbocharger an early 68 deg <br />\nbefore TDC and&nbsp; closes a late 50 deg after passing BDC.&nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n( Exhaust valve of 4th upward stroke remains open <br />\ntill 58 deg after TDC&nbsp; during fuel injection to displace <br />\nair for the incoming air + fuel .)</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nSTROKE 2 upwards COMPRESSION :--</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nAll valves are shut from 130 deg before TDC to allow <br />\ncompression.</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nSTROKE 3 downwards EXPLOSION:--</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nAll valves are shut till &nbsp;112 deg after TDC- then exhaust valve <br />\nopens to&nbsp;prevent loss of power due to back pressure .</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nSTROKE 4 upwards EXHAUST :--</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nExhaust valve opens an early 68 deg before BDC and shuts 58 <br />\ndeg after&nbsp;TDC- as a long arc for cooling too. &nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nREMARKS: ( may sound like pure baloney to the un-initiated! )</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nIf the fuel INTERFACE is is of very low vapourised flash <br />\npoint and very&nbsp;high cetane number , with NIL ignition lag , <br />\nthen it will PRE-ignite in&nbsp;a uncontrolled manner on stroke 1 <br />\ndue to residual heat ---- (instead of&nbsp;stroke 3 due to compression <br />\nheat ) when the exhaust valve is open thus&nbsp;losing a large <br />\npercentage of power. &nbsp;Our injection at 7.5 deg before TDC&nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nhowever is sufficiently late ( usually it is 16 ).</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nThe upward compression stroke NO 2 will have excessive load <br />\non conrods .&nbsp;&nbsp;The heat of compression will be excessive.<br />\nExplosion will take place&nbsp;before TDC, with slowing effect <br />\non crankshaft.</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nStroke no 3 downwards will be exploding with effective less <br />\nvolume air (&nbsp;which is hot ) with shorter ignition lag thus <br />\nlosing power. &nbsp;Volumetric&nbsp;efficiency will be around 50 % <br />\ninstead of 85%. &nbsp;Combustion heat&nbsp;converted to useful work <br />\nwill be only about 20%-- instead of the usual&nbsp;33% &nbsp;. <br />\nCrankcase deposits will increase. &nbsp;Carbon monoxide will be <br />\nformed&nbsp;in the exhaust gases.</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nExhaust temperatures will increase. Crankshaft turning will <br />\nbe un-uniform due to knocking . &nbsp;Main journal caps will <br />\ntake a beating on the&nbsp;4th upward exhaust stroke. &nbsp;it <br />\nwont be a constant pressure cycle.&nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nNIL SULPHUR MEANS -- NIL LUBRICATION FOR PLUNGERS AND <br />\nBARRELS-- WITH NO&nbsp; LUB ADDITIVE TO COMPENSATE. &nbsp;VERY LOW <br />\nVISC MEANS LEAKAGE PAST PLUNGER&nbsp; AND BARREL WITH LESS <br />\nINJECTION PRESSURE.&nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nbrgds</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\ncapt. ajit vadakayil</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nMASTER &nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nM.T. gas <br />\n( fluid film ) lubricant&nbsp;is compressible and of low viscosity ,<br />\nwith NIL deposits left over.</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nbunkers are rated by viscosity index. the lesser the viscosity is&nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nchanged by temperature, the higher the VI.</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nsolid marine lubricant molybedenum di sulphide scores <br />\nover graphite ,&nbsp;though it has the same inert quality and <br />\nthermal stability. for graphite&nbsp;without water is abrasive.</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nCHECK OUT THE ATTACHMENT:</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nno prizes for guessing what happened to the plunger <br />\nand barrel--&nbsp;immediately after changing over to low <br />\nsulphur fuel bunkered at Brazil ,&nbsp; from high sulphur fuel.</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nsuch things keep happening world wide. but them , <br />\nwhen we have mediocre&nbsp; people writing IMO circulars, <br />\nSOLAS and MARPOL&nbsp;-- what do you expect?</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nbrgds</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\ncapt. ajit vadakayil</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nMASTER &nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\nM.T. Ajit Vadakayil December 6, 2016 at 1:49 PM<br />IMPORTANT....... IMPORTANT...... IMPORTANT.......... THE WARSHIP INS BETWA , CAPSIZED WHILE UNDOCKING FROM DRYDOCK , DUE TO STABILITY CALCULATIONS NOT BEING DONE PROPERLY ..................... I AM A SHIP CAPTAIN WITH 30 YEARS EXPERIENCE ............. VIRTUAL LOSS OF GM DUE TO UPTHRUST .................... To calculate virtual loss of GM :-............. P= t X MCTC/ LCF ( t is trim in cms )....... virtual loss of GM= PX KM/W ( where W is displacement in tonnes ).............&nbsp;<span style=\"color: blue;\">Not many people realise that KM reduces with increase of trim................this is the reason why docking/ undocking trim by stern must be as small as possible\u2026\u2026\u2026.. while undocking the most critical and dangerous period is when the ship is afloat with only the aftermost part of keel resting on the aftermost block</span>\u2026\u2026\u2026\u2026 \u2026\u2026\u2026\u2026..FIRST STEP TO SALVAGE THE PATHETIC INDIAN NAVY IS TO CHANGE THE COLOUR OF THEIR UNIFORM FROM WHITE TO KHAKHI............. ALL RESPONSIBLE PEOPLE INCLUDING THE CAPTAIN MUST BE SACKED......... THIS IS SHEER INCOMPETENCE...........&nbsp;<span style=\"color: purple;\">The interval of time between the stern post landing on the blocks and the ship taking the blocks overall is referred to as the critical period....... During this period part of the weight of the ship is being borne by the blocks, and this creates an upthrust at the stern which increases as the water level falls in the drydock. ......The upthrust causes a virtual loss in metacentric height and it is essential that positive effective metacentric height be maintained throughout the critical period, or the ship will heel over and perhaps slip off the blocks with disastrous results.&nbsp;</span>....capt ajit vadakayil ..<br /><span style=\"color: red;\"><br />http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.in/2011/08/india-stands-tall-capt-ajit-vadakayil.html</span><br /><br />############################<br /><br />WE ASK NIRMALA SITARAMAN TO ADDRESS THE PROBLEM NOW .. PM MODI MUST BE PERSONALLY INVOLVED...<br /><br />OUR NAVAL OFFICERS LACK CHARACTER AND COMPETENCE... margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">The Scharnow turn is the fastest and the best when the point to be reached is significantly further astern than the vessel's turning radius, as is always the case. &nbsp;</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 6.0pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Put the rudder over hard. &nbsp;Take a wind assisted turn , to pick up momentum.&nbsp;&nbsp;This means with aft accommodation you will turn to port if the wind is from your port beam --as the aft accommodation acts like a huge mizzen sail.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 6.0pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Don\u2019t bother about the cardinal &nbsp;response to a man overboard, ie-- put the rudder toward the person (<i>e.g.</i>, if the person fell over the starboard side, put the rudder over hard to starboard).<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 1.2pt; margin-left: 38.4pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; tab-stops: list .5in; text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">1.<span style=\"font: normal normal normal 7pt/normal 'Times New Roman';\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span><span style=\"color: black; font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">After deviating from the original course by about 240 degrees, shift the rudder hard to the opposite side.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 1.2pt; margin-left: 38.4pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; tab-stops: list .5in; text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">2.<span style=\"font: normal normal normal 7pt/normal 'Times New Roman';\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span><span style=\"color: black; font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">When heading about 20 degrees short of the reciprocal course, put the rudder amidships so that vessel will turn onto the reciprocal course.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 6.0pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Always bring the vessel upwind of the person. Stop the vessel in the water with the person well forward of the ship\u2019s propeller.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 6.0pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">If the man in the water is swimming or has held on to the lifebuoy, try to get him grab on to a gangway net, and then up the pilot ladder or haul him up by a small bunker davit or crane.&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 6.0pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">You cant lower the rescue boat in rough seas. You can even use the LTA, connected to a long heaving line, and pull him in.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 6.0pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUkWuaFmHjI/AAAAAAAADQk/MTV-y59bZm8/s1600/CAPT_VADAKAYIL.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TUkWuaFmHjI/AAAAAAAADQk/MTV-y59bZm8/s1600/CAPT_VADAKAYIL.jpg\" /></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 6.0pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 6.0pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">..</span></div></div></div></div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "10", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/3223311548257439112/comments"}}], "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/MjAxOS0wNC0yMlQxMTozNzoyOS43MjRa\""}
